"system", "simplifi", "code"], "B_title": "Removed redundant code after ternary conditional", "B_clean_title": ["remov", "redund", "code", "after", "ternari", "condit"], "A_body": "The code for the current multi-language system is unnecessarily complex. This PR tries to improve on #5135 and simplify the code further.\n### Goal\n\nThis PR tries to achieve 4 goals:\n1. Remove a few inconsistencies in the code that may have resulted in hard-to-find bugs.\n2. Improve performance by moving the language-URL-behavior from several different *HelperRoute classes into the single plugin.\n3. Allow the routing code to work with the language data where necessary in order to simplify the code there, too.\n4. Allow for correct URLs and moving between languages where this is expected.\n\nEspecially the last part should be discussed in this PR. The new code does not force you to always use one specific language, but allows you to switch between them. The behavior should be the following:\n- If a user accesses a site for the first time, the plugin looks up if it should simply direct to the default language or try to discover the right language via the browser.\n- The language of the page is always determined by the URL.\n- On each pageload, a cookie is set with the current language. If a page has no attached language information, the data from the cookie is taken, otherwise the URL overrides that cookie.\n\nThis means that a user that surfs a french website and then clicks on a link to a specific english page on the site, the user is not redirected to a french page with the english content inside or an error page or similar.\n### How to test\n\nSimply apply the changes included in here and see that the URLs stay the same and the behavior for language handling is the way you expect it.\n### Routing changes\n\nThe above mentioned routing changes are primarily aimed at easing the code in other parts of Joomla. Currently, a URL is first created via a *HelperRoute class, which replaces the ISO language code from the content item with the corresponding SEF code. The language plugin, which right now is run before every other code in the routing process, takes that SEF code, compares it to the existing SEF codes, looks up the right language for it and then takes the SEF code from that language and adds it as part of the path in the URL. After that, it deletes the language code from the query, so that it is not available to the rest of the routing process anymore. Since the language is an important part of looking up the right Itemid, this means that the lookup of that part has to stay in the *HelperRoute class, instead of moving it to the component router itself.\n### Notice\n\nI changed the above description massively on January 3rd, 2015 in order to make it better understandable. Issue Tracker item #33627\n", "A_clean_body": ["joomla", "issu", "tracker", "item", "33627"], "B_body": "### Issue\n\nThere is a phpcs issue with the signature of `JHtmlSelect::suggestionlist()`. It contains a required `$idtag` after the optional `$optkey` and `$optText`, which essentially makes those two required as well.\n\nFixing this correct is basically not possible without creating a new function and proxy it.\n\nThe produced datalist also has some errors in it.\n### Solution\n- This PR will deprecate `JHtmlSelect::suggestionlist()` which was introduced with J3.2 to implement the `<datalist>` tag into the text formfield.\n- The datalist will be created directly in the `getInput()` function of the formfield instead. It's a very simple code and the current usage of `JHtmlSelect::options()` within `JHtmlSelect::suggestionlist()` to generate the items created more problems and was basically overkill.\n- Deprecated `getSuggestions()` in the text formfield and replaced it with `getOptions()` like we use in every other formfield. `getSuggestions()` is proxied to `getOptions()` in case someone was extending the class and actually used it.\n### Testing\n\nAdd some options to a text field and see if the datalist works. For example change the title for the article form to\n\n```\n        <field name=\"title\" type=\"text\" label=\"JGLOBAL_TITLE\"\n            description=\"JFIELD_TITLE_DESC\"\n            class=\"input-xxlarge input-large-text\"\n            size=\"40\"\n            required=\"true\" \n            >\n            <option>Option1</option>\n            <option value=\"Value2\">Option2</option>\n            <option value=\"Value3\" />\n        </field>\n```\n\nIt should show a list with \"suggestions\" as soon as you start typing or click into the field.\nPlease note that the first option will not show because there is no value given. The second option will show with both the value and the text, depending on browser (Chrome shows the text rigth aligned a bit smaller). "anoth", "languag"], "A_body": "Fixes gh-5179\n# Technical description\n\nThe libraries/classmap.php file registers class aliases with JLoader. This works fine when a developer creates an object using the old class name (e.g. JRegistry) instead of the new class (e.g. Joomla\\Registry\\Registry). However, this causes an issue when PHP doesn't try to autoload a class, e.g. when the old class name is in the right hand side of instanceof. Example:\n\n`$foo = new \\Joomla\\Registry\\Registry();\nvar_dump($foo instanceof \\Joomla\\Registry\\Registry); // returns true\nvar_dump($foo instanceof JRegistry); // returns false`\n\nHowever, if you have forced the autoloader to run you have no problem. Example:\n\n`$foo = new \\Joomla\\Registry\\Registry();\nclass_exists('JRegistry', true); // Dummy line just to force the autoloader to run\nvar_dump($foo instanceof \\Joomla\\Registry\\Registry); // returns true\nvar_dump($foo instanceof JRegistry); // returns true now!!!`\n\nWe can't use static `class_alias()` calls because PHP needs to load the original class, causing memory and performance issues. Instead, we need a way to create the aliases on-the-fly, when either then old class is loaded (via the dynamic alias set in JLoader) or through the new namespaced class name (through Composer).\n\nThis patch uses a fork of the `\\Composer\\Autoload\\ClassLoader` class which calls `JLoader::applyAliasFor($class)` when loading a class. This allows us to register class aliases on the fly, when the new, namespaced class is being loaded. Moreover, the same trick is applied to all of the JLoader autoloaders. This results in perfect backwards compatibility while we are proceeding with the namespacing of the core code.\n# Backwards compatibility\n\nThis patch actually _fixes_ backwards compatibility :)\n# Performance impact\n\nI could not measure performance impact, not because of lack or try or incompetence but because of variance. Therefore I conclude that the performance impact is statistically not important. In layman's terms: it's so small you can't even separate it from the variance in page load times added by external factors such as filesystem caches, code caches, web server thread management etc.\n\nAs for the memory impact, it is about 0.2Kb per aliased class. Even with hundreds of classes the memory impact is miniscule compared to the core code memory footprint.\n", "A_clean_body": ["fix", "gh", "5179", "technic", "descript", "php", "librari", "classmap", js", "B_clean_title": ["add", "simpl", "version", "admin", "templat", "css", "js"], "A_body": "My proposal to implement @brianteeman suggestion of refresh assets after version updates.\n\nThis method creates two new methods to <code>JDocument</code> to allow to load versionable assets:\n\n``` PHP\npublic function addScriptVersion($url, $version = null, $type = \"text/javascript\", $defer = false, $async = false)\n```\n\nand:\n\n``` PHP\npublic function addStyleSheetVersion($url, $version = null, $type = \"text/css\", $media = null, $attribs = array())\n```\n\nThe CMS is able to handle assets versions automatically but third part developers can also specify the assets versions.\n\nExample to allow the system to automatically add version:\n\n``` PHP\n$doc->addScriptVersion('templates/' . $this->template . '/js/template.js');\n```\n\nExample to specify the asset version manually:\n\n``` PHP\n$doc->addScriptVersion('templates/' . $this->template . '/js/template.js', '1,87');\n```\n\nThe automatic version is generated only:\n- When the user session is created\n- On each page load when debug is enabled.\n\nSo in the normal mode it would be created only 1 time per user session instead of 1 per page load. The version is built with:\n\n``` PHP\n$mediaTag = md5($this->getLongVersion() . $config->get('secret') . $date->toSql());\n```\n\nIt uses Joomla! version + secret string in configuration + current date + time.\n\nIt also includes one extra check to not add mediatag to assets that already contain it. So in most cases in can directly replace <code>addScript</code> & <code>addStylesheet</code> methods.\n\nThis modifies JFactory to add the mediatag on document creation. I saw that JFactory is already using JVersion so it doesn't add additional dependencies. But with this same method we can do it outside JFactory (for example inside a template) with:\n\n``` PHP\n$doc->setMediatag('23424235346456');\n```\n\nAnyone can flush assets cache with:  \n\n``` PHP\n$app = JFactory::getApplication()->flushAssets();\n```\n\nThis pull request already includes the code to refresh assets in:\n1. In <code>finaliseUpgrade()</code> method triggered after upgrading joomla.\n2. The background to this is as follows:\n1. A lot of Fabrik users want to make lists more compact - since there is no custom.css in the standard Joomla admin templates, at present we are using locale-based CSS i.e. en-gb.css (how weird is that!!!) to achieve this. Custom.css would be a more standard way of achieving this, and will be more convenient when developing a multi-country web-site where admin users might change locale frequently to test how it looks/works.\n2. Clearly a user can change the basic css files for the template, however that will be overwritten when you apply a Joomla update.\n3. It was previously suggested that the way to achieve this is to copy the template e.g. create my-isis and make changes to the CSS there. Copying an Admin template just to change small CSS seems to me to be a little over-kill - and will then provide a potential minefield of incompatibility where you are using a copy of an old template against an updated rest of Joomla, and a maintenance overhead to re-copy and reapply the css changes every time there is a joomla update.\n\nThis is a small and simple change with little risk, so I am
